<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-870501651537100850 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=870501651537100850><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/161154369763409921/d760257b5ffd16af7a8fa7056574cc51.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(46,204,113) title=kahnwong data-user-id=161154369763409921>kahnwong</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Friday, July 30, 2021 12:02 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-870501651537100850>7/30/2021 12:02 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve><span class="chatlog__markdown-mention" title="spectre_789">@spectre_789</span> 
1) install python like you normally would on a linux distro
2) airflow container is where the tasks are executed. no airflow container, no tasks can be executed, unless you use airflow to call other services to run your task (by that it means if your airflow gets killed the tasks are still running on external services)</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=thumbsup><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=👍 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f44d.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>1</span></div></div></div></div></div></div>

Go&#39;s job opportunities are also increasing but not aligned with de, although, I have experience with k8s microservices and it might open up other opportunities than de. </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(52,152,219) title=soulreaper4. data-user-id=313683402744397844>SoulReaper</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, August 18, 2021 12:47 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-877579390861602846>8/18/2021 12:47 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Read online and heard a co-worker say that Scala is just a better version of Java. I want to upgrade our stack, or at least experiment.

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-886327313673912351 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=886327313673912351><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/144557078399287296/5874a884efddce6046081113905b83e7.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=bungatown data-user-id=144557078399287296>bungatown</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Saturday, September 11, 2021 4:08 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-886327313673912351>9/11/2021 4:08 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve><span class="chatlog__markdown-mention" title="andynelson817">@AndyNelson</span> could be useful to use something columnar like bigquery, redshift, snowflake, etc then

as columns increase in a table then query performance does not suffer as much if you dont end up using it since the blocks of data are organized by columns. so it only scans the blocks of data for the columns it needs

versus in row oriented databases your read query performance can suffer because it will still have to scan the whole block or page of data related to your record even if the columns are not used

in addition performing aggregations on the data will also be easier, and quicker due to columnar compression</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=thumbsup><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=👍 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f44d.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>1</span></div></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-886328099166376017 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=886328099166376017><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Saturday, September 11, 2021 4:11 PM">4:11 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>maintaining a table of custom columns might still be difficult though cause then for each client youll have to create a new table and require a lot of joins or just have 1 big table with a lot of custom columns but then itd also end up very wide too

might be easier to reorganize your data into a long dataset rather than a wide dataset to make it more flexible on values

for example create a table with 3 new columns (client, category, value)

then it will be flexible to N number of category additions since you wont have to create an explicit column for each new unique addition that a client has, but youll have to pivot it</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=thumbsup><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=👍 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f44d.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>1</span></div></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-886519839424921640 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=886519839424921640><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=rakkit. data-user-id=209245848960368641>rakkit.</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Sunday, September 12, 2021 4:53 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-886519839424921640>9/12/2021 4:53 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>We tried direct queries initially, our IT screamed at us as the replication node is essentially the backup node for the hospital recording system. I also have no input into the oracle stuff, it&#39;s not managed by us it&#39;s Cerner (yeah).
The replication is live, there&#39;s no latency of the system updates and the table updates besides the transactional processing. The sole limitation is the fact we use SSIS for the extract and load. Hence why I presumed utilising Kafka could work for the live stuff we need, which is a small percentage, most is fine on daily incremental updates.
Our other core issue is that there&#39;s no oversight of the pipeline, or rules. I&#39;ve built a bespoke system within sql itself noting dependencies and business rules applied for lineage of data, but the scale were at now it&#39;s not sustainable to maintain.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

Any thoughts? Or how would you approach such a problem differently? </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=i_._i data-user-id=113136451457146880>dean</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Friday, September 17, 2021 5:50 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-888527303569702932>9/17/2021 5:50 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>We use it, swapped from Alooma after they got acquired by GCP and killed Snowflake support. 

We use the MySQL connector to replicate ~6 prod and test RDS MySQL DBs to Snowflake. Only major issue we had was when we upgraded MySQL and that caused some sort of an issue with the binlogs and required a full resync from fivetran. Their support was helpful though, and we probably didn’t do all our full diligence testing the upgrade and making sure replication and the binlogs were in a good state before doing the upgrade either. 

It’s been sort of a black box, when things go wrong you don’t quite get the best visibility into it, but also 90% of the errors have just worked themselves out. The upgrade issue was the only one we’ve run into. No data integrity issues, dropped rows, nothing like what we would occasionally see with Alooma. 

Overall happy with it I’d say.</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Friday, September 17, 2021 5:52 PM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-888543429703913472 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=888543429703913472><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/97751494236848128/f8958b8da99b07774393c7c9e0fb3376.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/113136451457146880/0275ef289c9e7b6338d7b72e8f4f2fca.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=i_._i>dean</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'888527303569702932')"> We use it, swapped from Alooma after they got acquired by GCP and killed Snowflake support.

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-888545493687369749 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=888545493687369749><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/113136451457146880/0275ef289c9e7b6338d7b72e8f4f2fca.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/97751494236848128/f8958b8da99b07774393c7c9e0fb3376.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author style=color:rgb(52,152,219) title=mashuma>jp</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'888543429703913472')"> Thank you Dean! Super helpful to hear.
We currently use stitch data for a lot of stuff (which I find quite frustrating to use).

How are the pricing compared with other tools? Some good while ago I had found some info on it and it seemed rather expensive for what it did, e.g. starting from USD 5k a month or something. </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=i_._i data-user-id=113136451457146880>dean</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Friday, September 17, 2021 7:02 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-888545493687369749>9/17/2021 7:02 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Fivetran’s pricing is based on “monthly active rows” so if a row in a table gets touched, that would be considered “active” and something that consumes credits. 

Alooma had a slightly different pricing model (but still based on volume) that was worse for us based on our transactional use case, but I don’t really remember what it was and how much worse it was. We certainly didn’t switch away because of cost, we switched away because they dropped support for our target DB, but Fivetran has cost less overall. I think it would depend on your particular transactional use-case and how many rows get touched on a regular basis. 

I imagine that their pricing model probably gets more attractive the more connectors you use as well, since they do support a lot of sources. Even if each individual source costs a bit, not having to pay multiple vendors for the “extract” in ETL is nice… especially in enterprises with glacial procurement processes. My team only uses the MySQL connector, but I know there are others inside the company that use the Salesforce connector, maybe a few others and we’re all billed together. For a single connector… I dunno, you’d probably have to do the math on that one which it sounds like you are. <img

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-897601411959881769 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=897601411959881769><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/197025602044166144/aaaf9f4b36bb8e99c3fda0f1d83a6189.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=_darco data-user-id=197025602044166144>Darco</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Tuesday, October 12, 2021 6:47 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-897601411959881769>10/12/2021 6:47 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>At least in MSSQL, I use CTEs if I need recursion or if I absolutely have to use a view rather than a stored procedure, but otherwise I try to avoid them.   They were used heavily at a previous job, and I solved a lot of performance problems just converting CTEs to temp tables in stored procedures.  Obviously try it both ways and see which one has a better execution plan, but it seems like the optimizer is just not great at finding a good plan when CTEs are involved.  Subqueries depend on the situation <s>but often times put you into non-sargable territory.</s></span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Tuesday, October 12, 2021 8:38 PM">(edited)</span></div><div class=chatlog__reactions><div class=chatlog__reaction title=thumbsup><img class="chatlog__emoji chatlog__emoji--small" alt=👍 src=https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/twitter/twemoji@latest/assets/svg/1f44d.svg loading=lazy> <span class=chatlog__reaction-count>2</span></div></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-897618411255894038 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=897618411255894038><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/333780027852324864/dfaa9acd759942e954edb98c8aa9c886.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/197025602044166144/aaaf9f4b36bb8e99c3fda0f1d83a6189.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=_darco>Darco</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'897601411959881769')"> At least in MSSQL, I use CTEs if I need recursion or if I absolutely have to use a view rather than a stored procedure, but otherwise I try to avoid them.   They were used heavily at a previous job, and I solved a lot of performance problems just converting CTEs to temp tables in stored procedures.  Obviously try it both ways and see which one has a better execution plan, but it seems like the optimizer is just not great at finding a good plan when CTEs are involved.  Subqueries depend on the situation <s>but often times put you into non-sargable territory.</s> </span> <span class=chatlog__reply-edited-timestamp title="Tuesday, October 12, 2021 8:38 PM">(edited)</span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=edog364 data-user-id=333780027852324864>edog364</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Tuesday, October 12, 2021 7:55 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-897618411255894038>10/12/2021 7:55 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Out of curiosity, what kinds of sub queries would make it non-sargable that would be sargable with a temp table? Do you have a link to any reading on this?</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-897620768446349372 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=897620768446349372><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/197025602044166144/aaaf9f4b36bb8e99c3fda0f1d83a6189.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=_darco data-user-id=197025602044166144>Darco</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Tuesday, October 12, 2021 8:04 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-897620768446349372>10/12/2021 8:04 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I threw that into my comment at the last minute because I&#39;ve seen a lot of misused subqueries, but it&#39;s true that you can misuse temp tables as well.  It&#39;s hard to optimize a query you haven&#39;t seen.  I&#39;ll strike that from the record. If you do something like where &lt;column&gt; in (select ...), you&#39;re right that it has just as much chance of using an index as a join to a temp table.  It&#39;s when you&#39;re using a correlated subquery where it&#39;s executing the same query for every record that you really get into trouble, and that doesn&#39;t really have anything to do with the concept of sargability, so you were right to call me on that. <a href="https://www.sqlservice.se/sql-server-performance-death-by-correlated-subqueries/">https://www.sqlservice.se/sql-server-performance-death-by-correlated-subqueries/</a></span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Tuesday, October 12, 2021 8:36 PM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-897621984391872564 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=897621984391872564><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Tuesday, October 12, 2021 8:09 PM">8:09 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I feel more comfortable disparaging CTEs as a generality though. :-P.    They&#39;re arguably easier to read, but when I was tuning stored procedures containing a CTE, it was very often the source of the problem.  In general, if I can make the optimizer&#39;s job easier by breaking complex queries into parts, it&#39;s not a bad place to start with performance problems.</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Tuesday, October 12, 2021 8:11 PM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

What I&#39;m running:
 
    Windows 10    
    Python 3.8.11
    Java 1.8
    Pyspark 3.1.2 w/ Hadoop 2.7
    JDBC8

I don&#39;t have admin so I manually set the paths:

 <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--multiline nohighlight">   os.environ[&#39;HADOOP_HOME&#39;] = &#39;C:/users/spark3.1.2hadoop2.7/
    os.environ[&#39;SPARK_HOME&#39;] = &#39;C:/users/spark3.1.2hadoop2.7/
    os.environ[&#39;JAVA_HOME&#39;] = &#39;C:/program files/Java/jdk1.80_301</code>
<code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--multiline language-py">    findpsark.init(&#39;C:/users/spark3.1.2hadoop2.7/&#39;)
    findspark.find()

    import pyspark
    from pyspark.sql import SQLContext, SparkSession

setup:

    conf = pyspark.SparkConf()
    conf.set(&#39;spark.driver.extraClassPath&#39;, &#39;c:/users/my/jar/ojdbc8.jar&#39;)

    spark = SparkSession.build\
              .config(conf=conf)\
              .master(&quot;local&quot;)\
              .appName(&#39;Spark_Oracle_Connection&#39;)\
              .getOrCreate()

    driver = &#39;oracle.jdbc.OracleDriver&#39;
    url = &#39;jdbc:oracle:thin:@myinfo&#39;
    user = &#39;user&#39;
    password = &#39;pass&#39;
    table=&#39;schema_table&#39;

    df.spark.read.format(&#39;jdbc&#39;)\
    .option(&#39;driver&#39;,driver)\
    .option(&#39;url&#39;,url)\
    .option(&#39;dtable&#39;,table)\
    .option(&#39;user&#39;, user)\
    .option(&#39;password&#39;,password).load()

    df.show()</code>
Everything prior works. It pulls my oracle table into a df.
